  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_027191e5-7058-43ab-abad-84827a76e802'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16768664798321416532">The narrator of  <em>The Zahir</em>  is a bestselling novelist who lives in Paris and enjoys all the privileges money and celebrity bring. His wife of ten years, Esther, is a war correspondent who has disappeared along with a friend, Mikhail, who may or may not be her lover.<br/><br/>Was Esther kidnapped, murdered, or did she simply escape a marriage that left her unfulfilled? The narrator d</span>
  <span id="freeText16768664798321416532" style="display:none">The narrator of  <em>The Zahir</em>  is a bestselling novelist who lives in Paris and enjoys all the privileges money and celebrity bring. His wife of ten years, Esther, is a war correspondent who has disappeared along with a friend, Mikhail, who may or may not be her lover.<br /><br />Was Esther kidnapped, murdered, or did she simply escape a marriage that left her unfulfilled? The narrator doesn’t have any answers, but he has plenty of questions of his own. Then one day Mikhail finds the narrator and promises to reunite him with his wife. In his attempt to recapture a lost love, the narrator discovers something unexpected about himself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16768664798321416532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_816723').observe('prototip:shown', function () {

          });

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/163758-my-heart-was-set-on-believing-his-stories">My heart was set on believing his stories. I am from Kazakhstan, and I am ethnically half Kazakh and lived in the country during Soviet times. All of the story of Mikhail can not be true, not even close. It shows the authors personal agenda to describe/criticize what he does not know, never experienced himself and failed to get the facts. Whether he is positive or negative, it screams lack of facts, ideas, knowledge.</a>
</div>

I read your comments, i would agree with you and i would like to add my comments to you. I feel his journey is more internal rather than going places. <div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/82427785-samantha-ege"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1531430569i/82427785._UX100_CR0,38,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/82427785-samantha-ege">Samantha Ege</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It shows how love isn't always perfect like the fairytales we have all grown up with, but it's disappointing due to the harsh reality of how emotional<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It shows how love isn't always perfect like the fairytales we have all grown up with, but it's disappointing due to the harsh reality of how emotionally unavailable the protagonist is and how vague and confusing his wife is. Although those are both stereotypical versions of men and women, I think it's pessimistic on how a relationship can and should be. Both characters don't fit with each other, and they see that in some retrospect. It was realistic, but pessimistic.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <span id="freeText932368023732704848" style="display:none">I believe the quotation below will be sufficient to show how brilliant Coelho is: <br /><br />‘Marie, let’s suppose that two firemen go into a forest to put out a small fire. Afterwards, when they emerge and go over to a stream, the face of one is all smeared with black, while the other man’s face is completely clean. My question is this: which of the two will wash his face? <br /><br />‘That’s a silly question. The one with the dirty face of course.’ <br /><br />‘No, the one with the dirty face will look at the other man and assume that he looks like him. And, vice versa, the man with the clean face will see his colleague covered in grime and say to himself: I must be dirty too. I’d better have a wash.’ <br /><br />‘What are you trying to say?’ <br /><br />‘I’m saying that, during the time I spent in the hospital, I came to realize that I was always looking for myself in the women I loved. I looked at their lovely, clean faces and saw myself reflected in them. They, on the other hand, looked at me and saw the dirt on my face and, however intelligent or self-confident they were, they ended up seeing themselves reflected in me thinking that they were worse than they were. Please, don’t let that happen to you.’ <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10160907332321888426">O Zahir = The Zahir, Paulo Coelho<br/>The Zahir is a 2005 novel by the Brazilian writer Paulo Coelho. Just as in an earlier book, The Alchemist, The Zahir is about a pilgrimage. The book touches on themes of love, loss and obsession. The Zahir was written in Coelho's native language, Portuguese, and it has been translated into 44 languages. The Zahir means 'the obvious' or 'conspicuous' in Arabic. The story revolves around the life of the narrator, a novelist, and in particular his search for his mis</span>
  <span id="freeText10160907332321888426" style="display:none">O Zahir = The Zahir, Paulo Coelho<br />The Zahir is a 2005 novel by the Brazilian writer Paulo Coelho. Just as in an earlier book, The Alchemist, The Zahir is about a pilgrimage. The book touches on themes of love, loss and obsession. The Zahir was written in Coelho's native language, Portuguese, and it has been translated into 44 languages. The Zahir means 'the obvious' or 'conspicuous' in Arabic. The story revolves around the life of the narrator, a novelist, and in particular his search for his missing wife, Esther. He enjoys all the privileges that money and celebrity bring. He is suspected of foul play by both the police and the press, who suspect that he may have had a role in the inexplicable disappearance of his wife from their Paris home.<br /><br />عنوانها: زهیر، ظاهر؛ نویسنده: پائولو کوئیلو؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز نخست ماه مارس سال 2004 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: زهیر؛ نویسنده: پائولو کوئیلو؛ مترجم: آرش حجازی؛ تهران، کاروان، چاپ دوم 1384، در 436 ص؛ شابک: 9648497303؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان برزیلی - سده 20 م<br />عنوان: ظاهر، مترجم: سوسن اردکانی؛ تهران، نگارستان کتاب، 1385، شابک: 9648155402؛ در 420 ص؛ <br />عنوان: زهیر، مترجم: دل آرا قهرمان؛ تهران، نشر فرزان روز، 1394؛ در 329 ص؛ شابک: 9789643214319؛ <br />عنوان: زهیر، مترجم: زهره معصومی؛ مشهد، آوای رعنا، 1396؛ در 350 ص؛ شابک: 9786007725009؛ <br /><br />نقل از کتاب: دو آتش نشان وارد جنگلی میشوند، تا آتش کوچکی را خاموش کنند. آخر کار وقتی از جنگل بیرون میآیند و میروند کنار رودخانه، صورت یکیشان کثیف و پر از خاکستر، و صورت آن یکی به شکل معصومانه ای تمیز است. پرسش: کدامشان صورتش را میشوید؟ اشتباه کردید، آن که صورتش کثیف است، به آن یکی نگاه میکند، و فکر میکند صورت خودش هم همان طور است. اما آن که صورتش تمیز است میبیند که سرتاپای رفیقش را غبار گرفته است، و به خودش میگوید: حتما من هم کثیفم، باید خودم را تمیز کنم. پایان نقل. در این رمان «پائولو» ضمن اشارات فراوان به زندگی شخصی خویش، داستانی بسیار شجاعانه ارائه داده، آکنده از عناصری که هر خوانشگری را به بازاندیشی در کنش و باورهای خود وامی‌دارد. راوی (نویسنده) همسرش را دوست دارد. همسرش ناپدید میشود و ردی از او نمیماند... از او فقط زهیر میماند. زهیر با یک نظر یا فکر گذرا شروع میشود، اما ذهن و روح انسان را تسخیر میکند. نویسنده ای مشهور ‍پی میبرد که همسرش که خبرنگار جنگ است، ناپدید شده و اثری از او نیست. هرچند گذر زمان برای این نویسنده موفقیت بیشتر و عشقی تازه به همراه میآورد، اما غیبت همسرش او را سرگشته نگه میدارد. چه بر سر همسرش آمده؟ او را دزدیده اند، کشته اند، یا فقط از زندگی زناشویی اش خسته شده و رفته؟ جستجوی نویسنده به دنبال همسرش --؛ و حقیقت زندگی خودش -- او را از فرانسه به اس‍پانیا، کرواسی و سرانجام دشتهای غم انگیز و زیبای آسیای میانه میکشاند و فراتر، او را از محیط امن دنیای خودش به جاده ای کاملا ناشناخته میبرد، به دنبال ادراکی تازه از معنای عشق و قدرت سرنوشت. ا. شربیانی</span>

  <span id="freeText15126011791082649559" style="display:none">So far my least favorite of Coelho's books. A woman leaves her husband with no explanation to find out how to be happy. And love changes the laws of nature."<br /><br />"Love is an untamed force. When we try to control it, it destroys us. When we try to imprison it, it enslaves us. When we try to understand it, it leaves us feeling lost and confused."<br /><br />"The most important thing in a ll human relationships is conversation, but people don't talk anymore, they don't sit down to talk and listen"</span>

<div id="review_398342324" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/398342324" />
    <a title="Rusalka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6163718-rusalka"><img alt="Rusalka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591511894p2/6163718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007204311" href="/book/show/212627.The_Zahir">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer398342324&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer398342324" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3268818306634952562">1 star. Self-congratulatory, conceited wankery. Only earns it's 1 as the prose was easy to read and well written for what it was. If you would like to read a book about how fantastic Coelho thinks he is, this is for you.<br/><br/>-------------<br/>By demand, my blog post on this book:<br/>-------------<br/><br/>I am just going to come out and say it.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/566.Paulo_Coelho' title='Paulo Coelho' rel='nofollow noopener'>Paulo Coelho</a> is a knob.<br/><br/>I dislike this man, his opinions and his writing. I have read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/865.The_Alchemist' title='The Alchemist by Paulo Coelho' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Alchemist</a> and the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4005.The_Fifth_Mountain' title='The Fifth Mountain by Paulo Coelho' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fifth Mountain</a> in the past and have felt that they were completely </span>
  <span id="freeText3268818306634952562" style="display:none">1 star. Self-congratulatory, conceited wankery. Only earns it's 1 as the prose was easy to read and well written for what it was. If you would like to read a book about how fantastic Coelho thinks he is, this is for you.<br /><br />-------------<br />By demand, my blog post on this book:<br />-------------<br /><br />I am just going to come out and say it.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/566.Paulo_Coelho" title="Paulo Coelho" rel="nofollow noopener">Paulo Coelho</a> is a knob.<br /><br />I dislike this man, his opinions and his writing. I have read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/865.The_Alchemist" title="The Alchemist by Paulo Coelho" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alchemist</a> and the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4005.The_Fifth_Mountain" title="The Fifth Mountain by Paulo Coelho" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Mountain</a> in the past and have felt that they were completely over rated. Then a friend links all these "insightful" quotes from him all the time on Facebook. And then there is <a href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/books/2012/aug/06/paulo-coelho-james-joyce-ulysses?INTCMP=SRCH" rel="nofollow noopener">this article</a> from earlier this month. But all of these were forgivable. Until I read this book. This book lead me to one conclusion.<br /><br />Paulo Coelho is a complete wanker.<br /><br />This book, The Zahir, is about an amazing author who is famous, incredibly successful with the ladies, intelligent, accomplished, and did I mention a brilliant writer? Maybe I need to tell you again how good a writer the author is. He is married, but has many girlfriends as he is incredibly attractive, and his wife who is a journalist goes missing. He mopes for a bit, while being a brilliant, amazing writer, but then gets an actress girlfriend. He then gets approached by a man who knows where his wife is, and he has to rediscover himself, by writing another ground-breaking book and some other stuff, before he can go find her. But the actress stays with him until he leaves, because he's great.<br /><br />In case you forget how wonderful he is, he points out randomly how many languages (nearly all the languages in the world) he has been translated into. The books themselves, while wonderful, are not him or his ideas. 'Everything that's written in my books is part of my soul...' (p101). Yeah right. Get your hand off it.<br /><br />Also he mentions the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_prison_experiment" rel="nofollow noopener">Zimbardo prison experiment</a> at one stage, because he can. Why? No idea. It wasn't important or necessary. It was in fact completely out of place, not to mention wrong, and seemed to be mentioned to show off how intelligent he was.<br /><br />My "favourite" part, was after he came home from spending all night out wandering Paris with the "Tribe" and then come home and didn't want to turn on the tv because they had "run out of things to talk about" so were covering a story of a rebellion in Haiti. So he goes on this whole rant about how is a rebellion important to him as a rich, incredibly successful author in Paris! Who cares! I just wanted to slap him the narrow minded prick! Urgh.<br /><br />As well as all of this he seems incredibly unhinged as well. He screams at his girlfriend after being out all night with the Tribe, mentioned above, and she doesn't ask him where he was. So therefore as she is not jealous (not interested, jealous) he screams at her for not loving him any more. Besides the fact he has been moaning on about his wife who he loves who has left him for the whole book. I was beyond loving him at p5, no wonder the girlfriend seemed to have had enough by p200. But she hadn't really. She really thought he was great. You know why? Because this unnamed author is fucking fantastic, just ask him.<br /><br />Why did I finish it? Because I wanted to find out what happened to his wife and girlfriend as I liked them (not worth it, it ended all about him), it was only 270pp, and it was orange (for a rainbow challenge). It gets 1.5 stars as it was well written for self-congratulatory masturbation. Actually, no. After writing this, 1.<br /><br />Knob.<br /><br />For more reviews visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://rusalkii.blogspot.com.au/">http://rusalkii.blogspot.com.au/</a></span>

<div id="review_41710553" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41710553" />
    <a title="Reshma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/273383-reshma"><img alt="Reshma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1188139293p2/273383.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41710553?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reshma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reshma" href="/user/show/273383-reshma">Reshma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41710553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8208448323504230489">I have to say, at times I found myself obsessed with this book about obsession. At times, it didn't quite flow or seemed to bring in random points, but I felt like I just "got it" and completely understood where he was coming from. Coelho's words resonated deeply within me, and in fact, helped me to "see" and unlock some feelings that I haven't been able to understand for quite some time. In that sense, it was like an <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19501.Eat__Pray__Love' title='Eat, Pray, Love by Elizabeth Gilbert' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eat, Pray, Love</a> for me. Not to compare authors, literary styles, or anything l</span>
  <span id="freeText8208448323504230489" style="display:none">I have to say, at times I found myself obsessed with this book about obsession. At times, it didn't quite flow or seemed to bring in random points, but I felt like I just "got it" and completely understood where he was coming from. Coelho's words resonated deeply within me, and in fact, helped me to "see" and unlock some feelings that I haven't been able to understand for quite some time. In that sense, it was like an <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19501.Eat__Pray__Love" title="Eat, Pray, Love by Elizabeth Gilbert" rel="nofollow noopener">Eat, Pray, Love</a> for me. Not to compare authors, literary styles, or anything like that - I'm only making the comparison in terms of what both books evoked in me. So for those of who you weren't such fans of Ms. Gilbert's book, don't let that dissuade you from reading this one. <br /><br />A few quotes from the Zahir that I particularly liked were: <br /><br />"...I came to realize that I was always looking for myself in the women I loved." <br /><br />"...I had convinced myself that I could only be happy with her, not because I loved her more than anything and anyone in the world, but because I thought only she could understand me; she knew my likes, my eccentricities, my way of seeing the world.......I was used to seeing the world through her eyes." <br /><br />"...suffering occurs when we want other people to love us in the way we imagine we want to be loved, and not in the way that love should manifest itself - free and untrammeled, guiding us with its force and driving us on." <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_9547015" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9547015" />
    <a title="Clare" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/300173-clare"><img alt="Clare" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203784399p2/300173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer9547015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7361364016878321157">I was diasspointed with this and I would consider myself a fan of Paolo Coelho. I just don't think this lived up to his usual work. The plot was weak and there was a lot of annoying, sentimental stream-of-consciousness drivel about the meaning of love and the meaning of life. It's true that these are Coelho's usual themes but I think he's gotten a bit carried away with all the sentiment in this novel and forgotten the story in the process. The only thing that kept me reading until the end was my</span>
  <span id="freeText7361364016878321157" style="display:none">I was diasspointed with this and I would consider myself a fan of Paolo Coelho. I just don't think this lived up to his usual work. The plot was weak and there was a lot of annoying, sentimental stream-of-consciousness drivel about the meaning of love and the meaning of life. It's true that these are Coelho's usual themes but I think he's gotten a bit carried away with all the sentiment in this novel and forgotten the story in the process. The only thing that kept me reading until the end was my enduring hate of the main character....he's one of those 'love to hate him' characters.</span>

<div id="review_2942388119" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2942388119" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11255849-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565547225p2/11255849.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2942388119?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/11255849-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2942388119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11412280535283392919"><i>The Zahir</i> is "someone or something which, once we have come into contact with them or it, gradually occupies our every thought, until we can think of nothing else. This can be considered either a state of holiness or of madness." This, and the spellbinding dedication page to Coelho's wife, Christina, made me want to read this novel. Plus, the story initially lured me. A writer's war correspondent wife goes missing. At first he's treated like a suspect until it's determined that she wasn't abduct</span>
  <span id="freeText11412280535283392919" style="display:none"><i>The Zahir</i> is "someone or something which, once we have come into contact with them or it, gradually occupies our every thought, until we can think of nothing else. This can be considered either a state of holiness or of madness." This, and the spellbinding dedication page to Coelho's wife, Christina, made me want to read this novel. Plus, the story initially lured me. A writer's war correspondent wife goes missing. At first he's treated like a suspect until it's determined that she wasn't abducted. But where did she go and why did she leave him? Who did she leave with? The otherness of their relationship appeals. Imagine settling in with this book to see how the story ebbs and flows, to see where the self-revelatory journey takes the main character. Only to be disappointed later.<br /><br /><blockquote>A year later, I wake thinking about the story by Jorge Luis Borges, about something which, once touched or seen, can never be forgotten, and which gradually so fills our thoughts that we are driven to madness. My Zahir is not a romantic metaphor - a blind man, a compass, a tiger, or a coin. It has a name, and her name is Esther.</blockquote><br /><br />This book doesn't end the way you would think. In fact, what happens in between this search, what the narrator uncovers, isn't what you would have envisioned. The events that center around spirituality and self actualization, events that center around the energy placed into the world by certain thoughts or actions, sometimes come across as trivial, and in some instances, forced. And those restaurant scenes, how people who live in poverty, and people who choose a different path in spiritual and physical life are depicted, were just exasperating. The gist is, a man is on a quest to love the wife he's undervalued for years (although he has a lover at home), and in this quest he meets people whose lives she's inspired, even if you don't truly get to see the evolution in these lives. I'm not sure which one bothered me the most: that the first part of the book didn't realistically set the plot, the continuous parables inside of dialogue, seeing the perspective of the character Mikhail often (instead of Esther's), the allusion to <i>the zahir</i> that didn't feel quite like one, and something else that I won't say because of spoilers. In any case, read if you simply want to try another Coelho book, or if you want to compare it to the last. Who knows, it could be your cup of tea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11412280535283392919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1341183252" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1341183252" />
    <a title="senjuti (센주티)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28061750-senjuti"><img alt="senjuti (센주티)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517899163p2/28061750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1341183252?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="senjuti (센주티)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="senjuti (센주티)" href="/user/show/28061750-senjuti">senjuti (센주티)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28061750-senjuti?shelf=paulo-coelho">paulo-coelho</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1341183252&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1341183252" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17450718999110977975">It took me a year to finish this book. There are two reasons- 1. I am too busy and 2. This book is indeed too lengthy, started with a simple incident (A famous writer living in Paris whose wife is a war correspondent. After being married for ten years, one day she left, without any trace.) and the writer clung to that incident and elongated (unnecessarily) the book. <br/>I started to read this book in spite of reading all sorts of negative reviews and ratings on Goodreads. I did not have high expecta</span>
  <span id="freeText17450718999110977975" style="display:none">It took me a year to finish this book. There are two reasons- 1. I am too busy and 2. This book is indeed too lengthy, started with a simple incident (A famous writer living in Paris whose wife is a war correspondent. After being married for ten years, one day she left, without any trace.) and the writer clung to that incident and elongated (unnecessarily) the book. <br />I started to read this book in spite of reading all sorts of negative reviews and ratings on Goodreads. I did not have high expectation from this book. I love to read Paulo Coelho's books because his books always give me some questions to think through. I read a number of his books. All the books promoted the same thing, yet they have different questions of their own. What I love about this book are the quotes. I loved this particular conversation. This was part of an interview which the wife of the writer, Esther took once. She was arguing with her husband about, people are not happy: <br />'No, what they say is: "When the children have grown up, when my husband- or my wife- has become more my friend than my passionate lover, when I retire, then I'll have time to do what I always wanted to do: travel." Question: "But didn't you say you were happy now? Aren't you already doing what you always wanted to do?" Then they say they are very busy and change the subject.' <br />This part got me thinking, am I happy with my life? I got no clear answer from my heart. Like the person that Esther interviewed, I have everything that a person can think of, and yet I think of doing something I always wanted to do. It's contradictory, isn't it?<br />Another favourite part of mine:<br />"Our children must follow in our footsteps: after all, we are older and know about the world.<br />We must have a university degree even if we never get a job in the area of knowledge we were forced to study.<br />We must study things that we will never use, but which someone told us important to know: algebra, trigonometry, the code of Hammurabi.<br />We must never make our parents sad, even if it means giving up everything that makes us happy."<br />This particular excerpt summarizes my life that I am leading now. When you are a depressed engineering student, all you love is some veracities from a foreign writer. Those veracities are your words written in the magic of another person, in this case, writer Paulo Coelho.<br />Therefore, if I cut through the re-iterating part of this book, this book is not at all that bad. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17450718999110977975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

But you cannot make a painting with a hammer, or a sculpture with a paintbrush. Therefore, however difficult it may be, I must accept today's small blessings, even if they seem like curses because I am suffering and it's a beautiful day, the sun is shining, and the children are singing in the street. This is the only way I will manage to leave my pain behind and rebuild my life."   <span id="freeText16248401711484211785" style="display:none">This book was nothing like I expected. The back description was misleading - as a novice traveller I saw that the narrator of the book was going to go through "Spain, France, Croatia" etc in order to find the love of his life. Do not be fooled, there is little to no description of these places. In fact, there is no description of Spain at all. Thoroughly disappointing. <br /><br />Besides that the book itself was... interesting. I admit it is a much different story than I have ever read and I was given some new ideas and thoughts. However I did not find the end fulfilling nor did I feel a great connection with the main character.</span>

<div id="review_473101688" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/473101688" />
    <a title="Dominic Carrillo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10598743-dominic-carrillo"><img alt="Dominic Carrillo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557343109p2/10598743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/473101688?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dominic Carrillo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dominic Carrillo" href="/user/show/10598743-dominic-carrillo">Dominic Carrillo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer473101688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4236829402047470263">I liked The Alchemist... And I liked a few other Coelho novels- especially if I happened to be reading them at just the right time in my life. I stopped reading The Zahir at pg. 200 because I couldn't take any more of the mystical, inner voice, follow-the-signs, journey-seeking cheeseball shit that seems to be this author's bread and butter. I admit, I've enjoyed Coelho at certain times and when in the right mood. But this time it came across to me as an author's regurgitation of the same theme,</span>
  <span id="freeText4236829402047470263" style="display:none">I liked The Alchemist... And I liked a few other Coelho novels- especially if I happened to be reading them at just the right time in my life. I stopped reading The Zahir at pg. 200 because I couldn't take any more of the mystical, inner voice, follow-the-signs, journey-seeking cheeseball shit that seems to be this author's bread and butter. I admit, I've enjoyed Coelho at certain times and when in the right mood. But this time it came across to me as an author's regurgitation of the same theme, repackaged so many times that the "wisdom" of his message is diluted down to bullshit or cliche adages. For two hundred pages I convinced myself to read more thinking it was bound to get better, somewhat original, and that the story might move a bit faster. I rarely quit reading a novel after making it more than half way through, but I'm putting this one to rest with no regret; no inner conflict; no mystical voice telling me to change my life's path. I have. But it makes me wonder how many times Coelho has, or if he's transformed himself so many times, that he's made a complete 360 many times over.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4236829402047470263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_132923516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132923516" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132923516?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Brad by: </span>
      Giovanna
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=philosophical">philosophical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132923516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4878650450350252999">This book wasn't written for me. I am not on a search for spirituality; I am not trying to understand my spirituality; I don't even think humanity itself is all that special, and I certainly don’t believe spirituality is what separates us from the beasts. So from the earliest moments of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1427.The_Zahir' title='The Zahir by Paulo Coelho' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Zahir</a> I felt like a tourist, an unwelcome voyeur. <br/><br/>But then this book <u>was</u> written for me because, stripping away all the talk of spirituality, I am looking for complete sensuality, complete living, complete be</span>
  <span id="freeText4878650450350252999" style="display:none">This book wasn't written for me. I am not on a search for spirituality; I am not trying to understand my spirituality; I don't even think humanity itself is all that special, and I certainly don’t believe spirituality is what separates us from the beasts. So from the earliest moments of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1427.The_Zahir" title="The Zahir by Paulo Coelho" rel="nofollow noopener">The Zahir</a> I felt like a tourist, an unwelcome voyeur. <br /><br />But then this book <u>was</u> written for me because, stripping away all the talk of spirituality, I am looking for complete sensuality, complete living, complete being and much of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1427.The_Zahir" title="The Zahir by Paulo Coelho" rel="nofollow noopener">The Zahir</a> was about accepting these possibilities in our lives. When <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/566.Paulo_Coelho" title="Paulo Coelho" rel="nofollow noopener">Coelho</a> was talking about these possibilities, I felt welcomed into the community of the book. The book felt right.<br /><br />I wondered how I was supposed to care about a man of leisure and the problems only he could afford to have. I disdained his dilettantism. The constant pontification concerning love drove me insane. I shook my head at the blindness of the narrator's faith -- in damn near everything. I loathed the constant lecturing about love and personal history. I was unsatisfied with the ending. <br /><br />Yet I was captivated by the questions the narrator asked, the way he had to know certain bits of minutia to be happy. I embraced the unconventional visions of love and fidelity. I cared what happened to Nobody and Mikhail/Oleg and Esther and Marie. I revelled in the literary references. I loved the narrative voice. I was compelled to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1427.The_Zahir" title="The Zahir by Paulo Coelho" rel="nofollow noopener">The Zahir</a> at pace. And I was paradoxically satisfied with the ending.<br /><br />I can't think of anyone I would recommend this book to, except maybe my friend Ruzz, but I wouldn't really tell anyone to stay away from this book either, except maybe my friend Ruzz. <br /><br />I am baffled by the experience. I am curious to read more of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/566.Paulo_Coelho" title="Paulo Coelho" rel="nofollow noopener">Coelho</a>'s work. I don't know if I will.<br /><br />I wonder if this reading experience will stick with me, or if all I will retain is my new found fascination with train tracks. I just don't know. Not at all.<br /><br />(Why did you give me this book, Giovanna?)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4878650450350252999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1566889251" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1566889251" />
    <a title="Marianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5067228-marianne"><img alt="Marianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303027210p2/5067228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1566889251?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marianne" href="/user/show/5067228-marianne">Marianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1566889251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16420803091994499840">The Zahir is the sixth stand-alone book by Brazil-born author, Paulo Coelho. It is translated from Portuguese by Margaret Jull Costa. Esther, a journalist and the wife of a best-selling author disappears from their home in Paris. Once the police release him from custody, dismissing the idea that he may have been responsible, he begins to wonder what has happened. He is soon convinced that she left him voluntarily, despite her occasionally dangerous job as a war correspondent. For two years, he r</span>
  <span id="freeText16420803091994499840" style="display:none">The Zahir is the sixth stand-alone book by Brazil-born author, Paulo Coelho. It is translated from Portuguese by Margaret Jull Costa. Esther, a journalist and the wife of a best-selling author disappears from their home in Paris. Once the police release him from custody, dismissing the idea that he may have been responsible, he begins to wonder what has happened. He is soon convinced that she left him voluntarily, despite her occasionally dangerous job as a war correspondent. For two years, he remains obsessed about learning the reason she left him. <br /><br />The first thing the narrator does is find himself a girlfriend. Then, suitably catered for sexually, he laments his inability to understand why his wife left him. As the narrator (eventually, after more than two years) sets about looking for her, the tale is filled with waffle about finding oneself, pure divine energy, spiritual journey, and energy of love flowing around the world. Much of it seems to be a vehicle for expressing the author’s opinion about topics like wealth, sex and fidelity, marriage, and power. <br /><br />From the narrator’s history it would seem that this story is largely autobiographical. The author must have quite some charisma in person, because on paper his attitude and arrogance are unappealing. The dialogue is wooden (although perhaps this is a function of the translation); the prose is dull; much of the story feels contrived. This book might appeal to men of a Latin background who fancy themselves on a spiritual journey. 2 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16420803091994499840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166113695" />
    <a title="Engy Moussa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4315794-engy-moussa"><img alt="Engy Moussa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298033881p2/4315794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166113695?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Engy Moussa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Engy Moussa" href="/user/show/4315794-engy-moussa">Engy Moussa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166113695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5340963445994807424">I am momentarily wordless.. But I will eventually have to say something, if not lots of things, on the exceptional Coelho’s novel The Zahir. I may begin by saying that this novel was like a textbook on real life and true love for me. It introduced me to many new concepts, such as personal history, as well as to many interesting anecdotes that I would pay anything to my memory so it always remembers them. I don’t think that I ever liked as many statements, at some points whole pages, in one book.</span>
  <span id="freeText5340963445994807424" style="display:none">I am momentarily wordless.. But I will eventually have to say something, if not lots of things, on the exceptional Coelho’s novel The Zahir. I may begin by saying that this novel was like a textbook on real life and true love for me. It introduced me to many new concepts, such as personal history, as well as to many interesting anecdotes that I would pay anything to my memory so it always remembers them. I don’t think that I ever liked as many statements, at some points whole pages, in one book. Coelho’s style, the emotions and sincerity he put in his writing mesmerized me from the first page till the last word in the book; and at last I refuse to let go of them although I am done with the novel. The story is unique and rich in its own way. It represents an extraordinary romance which evolves throughout the story despite the total separation between its holders. If life is a learning field then true love will be the hardest and toughest lesson to excel and protect. <br /><br />Engy Moussa<br />7/6/2011 at 22:47</span>

<div id="review_1420042978" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420042978" />
    <a title="Andreea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1417076-andreea"><img alt="Andreea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395578865p2/1417076.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1420042978?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea" href="/user/show/1417076-andreea">Andreea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1420042978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1424822027407679441">Can I give no star to this book? No? Okay. Let's start. I AM SO GLAD I FINALLY FINISHED IT because it was going on and on forever with no purpose. Why I hate it, you ask? Because it pretends to be something it's not and has an annoying main character. It's the best example for how not to write a book. You know the "show, don't tell" advice that writers give a lot? THIS BOOK IS ONLY SAYING AND TELLING AND HOPES THE WORDS BECOME SHOW. But you can't say the character changed and evolved (and it's n</span>
  <span id="freeText1424822027407679441" style="display:none">Can I give no star to this book? No? Okay. Let's start. I AM SO GLAD I FINALLY FINISHED IT because it was going on and on forever with no purpose. Why I hate it, you ask? Because it pretends to be something it's not and has an annoying main character. It's the best example for how not to write a book. You know the "show, don't tell" advice that writers give a lot? THIS BOOK IS ONLY SAYING AND TELLING AND HOPES THE WORDS BECOME SHOW. But you can't say the character changed and evolved (and it's not superficial anymore or blah blah) but he continues to act the way it always did. <br /><br />I do not hate unlikable main characters or anything, but only when they are portrayed that way intentionally. But I have a feeling the author (the book is a bit semi-autobiographical or something) actually believes this character is right and not the superficial d*ck he is!!!<br /><br />And another thing that annoys me is HOW EVERYONE AND THEIR MOTHER (and my mother, cause I read this book because she likes Coelho) pretend this author is some brilliant spiritual guy or something. Don't get me wrong, I have no problem with bad books being popular or bad writers being popular - hell, I really enjoy Dan Brown's novels - but usually those books know what they are and accept it and have no problem. But this guy and his books pretend to be the gem of the literature and the best creation ever. <br /><br />Ih! So glad I finished the book and I am pretty sure I will not make myself read another one of his books. Also, I know mum likes his books but I won't buy them any for her birthday because I do not want to support this guy - and she'll be happier if I get her cute oven mittens or a new hoover!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1424822027407679441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1420042978">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbana Kurti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbana Kurti" href="/user/show/92171335-barbana-kurti">Barbana Kurti</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2918736594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3899321046012873251">The Zahir in my opinion Is not a novel but a collection of “wise” quotations. The plot is weak and the characters have no development at all. It seems like the author forgot about the story and in the end he kind of remembered that he has to finish the plot. <br/><br/>The main character is arrogant has an excessive urge for admiration, entitled and idiotic. <br/>People think that being different equates to being better, that different thoughts mean better thoughts. that is mostly not true. Being different mean</span>
  <span id="freeText3899321046012873251" style="display:none">The Zahir in my opinion Is not a novel but a collection of “wise” quotations. The plot is weak and the characters have no development at all. It seems like the author forgot about the story and in the end he kind of remembered that he has to finish the plot. <br /><br />The main character is arrogant has an excessive urge for admiration, entitled and idiotic. <br />People think that being different equates to being better, that different thoughts mean better thoughts. that is mostly not true. Being different means you are just different and that’s about it, it’s not rocket science. <br /><br />When majority of people think a certain way there is a logical answer to why. The main character and all characters in general from this book try so hard to be special and different that they end up being all the same. <br /><br />I did not enjoy this book, however I am giving Coelho another chance and grab another book <br />written by him just because I liked this one quote : <br /><br />“Marie, let’s suppose that two firemen go into a forest to put out a small fire. Afterwards, when they emerge and go over to a stream, the face of one is all smeared with black, while the other man’s face is completely clean. My question is this: which of the two will wash his face? <br /> <br />That’s a silly question. The one with the dirty face of course.’ <br /> <br />No, the one with the dirty face will look at the other man and assume that he looks like him. And, vice versa, the man with the clean face will see his colleague covered in grime and say to himself: I must be dirty too. I’d better have a wash.’ <br /><br />I’m saying that, during the time I spent in the hospital, I came to realize that I was always looking for myself in the women I loved. I looked at their lovely, clean faces and saw myself reflected in them. They, on the other hand, looked at me and saw the dirt on my face and, however intelligent or self-confident they were, they ended up seeing themselves reflected in me thinking that they were worse than they were. Please, don’t let that happen to you.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="3899321046012873251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1864523561091423516">This book was not of the same quality as Alchemist but still presented some noble and elevated concepts as presented in all of paulo's books and perhaps the reason I read his books is that they always tend to feature some sort of spiritual quest. There is also a aspect of Sufism in Paulo's books which make them more eminent.<br/><br/>The unnamed narrator of this story is a writer whose wife, Esther, a war correspondent leaves him suddenly without any information or trace of leaving. When she disappears, h</span>
  <span id="freeText1864523561091423516" style="display:none">This book was not of the same quality as Alchemist but still presented some noble and elevated concepts as presented in all of paulo's books and perhaps the reason I read his books is that they always tend to feature some sort of spiritual quest. There is also a aspect of Sufism in Paulo's books which make them more eminent.<br /><br />The unnamed narrator of this story is a writer whose wife, Esther, a war correspondent leaves him suddenly without any information or trace of leaving. When she disappears, he is disturbed by the mystery of what has happened. Has she been killed, kidnaped, or left him for another love. The narrator starts his struggle to find the reason of Esther's disappearance and eventually he realizes that she is the one who fills his life with meaning.<br /><br />Coelho has not created a master work on the level of Alchemist but still there are some insights on courage needed to reach destiny, risks and possiblities of life and rewards of forgetting personal histories.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2376178259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376178259" />
    <a title="Marziye Foroughi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51177450-marziye-foroughi"><img alt="Marziye Foroughi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603991215p2/51177450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2376178259?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marziye Foroughi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marziye Foroughi" href="/user/show/51177450-marziye-foroughi">Marziye Foroughi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2376178259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15228833036299409096">I believe The Zahir is a chain of events with really great quotations rather than a novel because it has no climax, rising and falling action. It deals with Sufism, psychology and somehow magic realism. Its main themes are love, loss, obsession, marriage.<br/>Coelho's words resonated deeply within me and in fact, helped me to "see" and unlock some feelings that I haven't been able to understand for quite some time. <br/>you should know yourself before doing anything special in your life. this is the rule </span>
  <span id="freeText15228833036299409096" style="display:none">I believe The Zahir is a chain of events with really great quotations rather than a novel because it has no climax, rising and falling action. It deals with Sufism, psychology and somehow magic realism. Its main themes are love, loss, obsession, marriage.<br />Coelho's words resonated deeply within me and in fact, helped me to "see" and unlock some feelings that I haven't been able to understand for quite some time. <br />you should know yourself before doing anything special in your life. this is the rule I deeply believe in it after reading the Zahir.<br />I don't recommend this book to anyone who believes in traditional concepts of marriage.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15228833036299409096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ae6hH/KsTyI9i6cjeDoXYUR+XM4VWm+kaoVSzDmrnhiakVYqe1LMgt4a0fj/jcvjyMjagz0Wml8qURw8K5Yf6w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Zu07afS9MUqiEjPlVHwGLymdNVSbihDD8G4mv7CavmOVksxcfUOy6kGDRT7Ty9qtpSuzGbPG5TiwumhPoqc/kA==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/566.Paulo_Coelho">About Paulo Coelho</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/566.Paulo_Coelho"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1201840056p3/566.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/566.Paulo_Coelho">Paulo Coelho

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12044388723416772927">The Brazilian author PAULO COELHO was born in 1947 in the city of Rio de Janeiro. Before dedicating his life completely to literature, he worked as theatre director and actor, lyricist and journalist. In 1986, PAULO COELHO did the pilgrimage to Saint James of Compostella, an experience later to be documented in his book The Pilgrimage. In the following year, COELHO published The Alchemist. Slow in</span>
  <span id="freeText12044388723416772927" style="display:none">The Brazilian author PAULO COELHO was born in 1947 in the city of Rio de Janeiro. Before dedicating his life completely to literature, he worked as theatre director and actor, lyricist and journalist. In 1986, PAULO COELHO did the pilgrimage to Saint James of Compostella, an experience later to be documented in his book The Pilgrimage. In the following year, COELHO published The Alchemist. Slow initial sales convinced his first publisher to drop the novel, but it went on to become one of the best selling Brazilian books of all time. Other titles include Brida (1990), The Valkyries (1992), By the river Piedra I sat Down and Wept (1994), the collection of his best columns published in the Brazilian newspaper Folha de São Paulo entitle Maktub (1994), the compilation of texts Phrases (1995), The Fifth Mountain (1996), Manual of a Warrior of Light (1997), Veronika decides to die (1998), The Devil and Miss Prym (2000), the compilation of traditional tales in Stories for parents, children and grandchildren (2001), Eleven Minutes (2003), The Zahir (2005), The Witch of Portobello (2006) and Winner Stands Alone (to be released in 2009). During the months of March, April, May and June 2006, Paulo Coelho traveled to celebrate the 20th anniversary of his pilgrimage to Saint James of Compostella in 1986. He also held surprise book signings - announced one day in advance - in some cities along the way, to have a chance to meet his readers. In ninety days of pilgrimage the author traveled around the globe and took the famous Transiberrian train that took him to Vladivostok. During this experience Paulo Coelho launched his blog Walking the Path - The Pilgrimage in order to share with his readers his impressions. Since this first blog Paulo Coelho has expanded his presence in the internet with his daily blogs in Wordpress, Myspace &amp; Facebook. He is equally present in media sharing sites such as Youtube and Flickr, offering on a regular basis not only texts but also videos and pictures to his readers. From this intensive interest and use of the Internet sprang his bold new project: The Experimental Witch where he invites his readers to adapt to the screen his book The Witch of Portobello. Indeed Paulo Coelho is a firm believer of Internet as a new media and is the first Best-selling author to actively support online free distribution of his work. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12044388723416772927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
